ªÇæ ÄÍå®åÚÆ ºøÌàÌ ºåÇ¸ ÄÍºå (¼ñå Íå ºå¨àË¸¡ÄåºñºëÄå)(ºÇ®ÚºÈÐ (Í¹¼Ç±È¼È»¼Æ) ¶ÈÃ ¶Ç¼µ - ³Æ³Ç¸"Ì¶ÇÀÈ¾ÆØ´Æ¹»¾Æ £Îº±Æ±¼Æ)(The Hon. (Prof.) Tissa Vitharana - Minister of Science andTechnology)ªÇæ ¨»å¾åÆ¨ºëÄ¾è, £ïÆà ÀåÚÈèï¾àºëï¼û ªÇæ ÄÈà ÑÇÉâÊ Ä¾àºòéºëÄåÆ Àò¨åÊÆ¨à ¨Îå, ÌÚÉ Àå¨àËè¨ ¾øïÆåàÔº ¨´êï ¨´ÆêºëÌÂ¾à½ïÆ¾à. ¦Æ ¾øÉæÇ¼ú ¨Ç¾à¾ ¡ÉÊñÆú. ÌèÆõÄ ÀåÚÈèï¾àºëÄ¾àºòéºëÄ¾àÈåïªà ¡ÉïÂåà½Æºà, ÌÍåÆºà Àº¾à Äå ïÄÆ ¼æ¾à ¢¼úÖÀºà ¨Ç¾Éå.

The Hon. Wimal Weerawansa stated on 22nd November,2006 in Parliament that the JVP did not agree to “devolution”at the All Party Representative Committee but agreed only todiscuss about it. I wish to correct this.

Dr. Vasantha Bandara, the JVP representative at the AllParty Representative Committee, stated that he supported“devolution” provided it was done properly to benefit thepeople. When I, as Chairman of the APRC, at the 17th meetingof the APRC summarized the views of the partyrepresentatives as being “support for devolution as the meansof solving the national question” , neither Dr. Bandara noranyone else objected. I thanked everyone for reaching aconsensus and Mr. Thavarajah of the EPDP expressed hiscongratulations for achieving a consensus. This is on record.I regret that the statement made by the Hon. WimalWeerawansa does not accord with the facts.

ÌÃåÀºøºëÄå(¶±Ç¿¼Æ £Á¼Æ¯¿Æ)(The Chairman)§ÂºëÄå Ì¼àÃåÉïÆ¾à ¨Ç¾ È¼ ï®¾ ÄÄ ¡ªÆ ¨Ç¾Éå.

2006 ï¾åÉæÂÚ 2310651066

ªÇæ ÍêïÌà¾à ¡ÍÄ ÂÆúÈå ÄÍºå (ÌæÈÌê Íå ÌæÈÌê ¨òèÆåºàÄ¨¨ø×ï ¾øïÆåà°ñ ¡Äåºñ)(ºÇ®ÚºÈÐ ÄÊÎÃ £Äº´Æ Î¹¾Ç - ¶È´Æ´ºÆ, ¶È´Æ´±ÆÌ±»½Æ¹Õ¶Æ ×Î¯ ¼¶È £Îº±Æ±¼Æ)(The Hon. Hussain Ahamed Bhaila - Deputy Minister of Plan andPlan Implementation)

Thank you, Mr. Chairman, for giving me this opportunityto speak a few words on the Votes of the Ministry of PlanImplementation, which is headed by His Excellency thePresident.

Before I proceed to speak in respect of my Ministry, I mustrefer to the Hon. Joseph Michael Perera’s speech. Hementioned of the power of the President to nominate orappoint the Prime Minister. While appreciating his right tosay what he wishes, I think it would be much better if, in thefirst place, the political parties are given the power to choosetheir own leader like they did in the Sri Lanka Freedom Party.When the majority of members wanted a new leader appointed,they elected His Excellency Mahinda Rajapaksa as thePresident of their party. Unfortunately, that does not seem tobe so in other parties which are now saying that there shouldbe more democracy. These so-called democratic rights havebeen taken away by the Constitution that had been preparedby the United National Party. Even the power to dissolveParliament after one year had been given to the President bythe Constitution that was promulgated by the United NationalParty. So, I do not think that they have any right today to talkabout the Executive powers that had been conferred on thePresident by that Constitution.

Also there was a mention about the Supreme Courtjudgments. We in this country hold the Supreme Court inthe highest esteem and we have conferred powers on it throughthe Constitution. We are not bound by whatever certainNGOs or international organizations talk about our judgments.I feel that they have absolutely no right to discuss thejudgments given by the highest court in our land.

The Hon. Joseph Michael Perera also mentioned about thedelay of the report of the Committee on Public Accounts onthe Auditor-General’s findings. I think he seems to haveforgotten the fact that the Chairmanship of the Committeeon Public Accounts has been given to the Opposition and atthe moment, it is headed by an Hon. Member of theOpposition.

He also mentioned about the Judicial Service Commission.Who is most competent to decide on the transfers of thejudiciary? Is it politicians like us or the Judicial ServiceCommission, which consists of members of the highestjudiciary, to whom we look up to and headed by that greatmember of the judiciary, Chief Justice Sarath N. Silva.

Mr. Chairman, moving on to my Ministry, today, for theinformation of the Hon. Members, we have distributed ourperformance report which highlights the work done by theMinistry so far. The subjects and functions assigned to the

Ministry are indeed onerous and we are conscious of the factthat an effective discharge of these functions will contributegreatly to the development of our country. The Ministry hasaccepted responsibility with the seriousness it deserves andis committed to give its best to achieve useful results. In thisendeavour, I am fortunate to have had at the beginning of theyear the services of Mr. Ajith Nivard Cabraal as the Secretaryand from mid-year, upon his moving to the very responsibleposition as Governor of the Central Bank, we have got onceagain an equally efficient officer, Mrs. Dhara Wijeyatilake,as the Secretary of our Ministry.

The Ministry of Plan Implementation, which has beenestablished as an independent Cabinet level Ministry onlyat the end of last year, has been working on ways and meansto carry out its functions. We have focused-

ÌÃåÀºøºëÄå(¶±Ç¿¼Æ £Á¼Æ¯¿Æ)(The Chairman)Order, please! §ÂºëÄå´ ¾øÆº ¨åÈÆ ¡ÉÌå¾Æú.

ªÇæ ÍêïÌà¾à ¡ÍÄ ÂÆúÈå ÄÍºå(ºÇ®ÚºÈÐ ÄÊÎÃ £Äº´Æ Î¹¾Ç)(The Hon. Hussain Ahamed Bhaila)

ªÇæ ï¨ïÍÎèÆ ÇÅê¨àÉæÈàÈ ¡ÄåºñºëÄåïªà ¨åÈïÆ¾à ¾å 5¨à Ä´Èæ ºøïÂ¾Éå.

We have focused this year on monitoring the developmentprogrammes and projects of the Government and looked atnew ways of ensuring better implementation of those. Weare conscious that while sound policies are essential to buildand develop a nation, so is effective implementation of suchpolicies.

We have placed particular emphasis on the major foreign-funded projects and the effective implementation of the“Mahinda Chintana.” We all are aware that political leadersgive various pledges and promises during election time.But thereafter, after being elected to office, those are allforgotten. But it is not so in the case of His ExcellencyMahinda Rajapaksa. It is here that the “Mahinda Chintana”,the Manifesto of His Excellency the President , makes a verybig difference in the country. The task of implementing whatis set out in this document has been especially assigned byHis Excellency the President to this Ministry as a specificsubject and he retains control of this Ministry as the Minister.The Plan of Action, which has been drawn up on the basis ofthe “Mahinda Chintana”, has received Cabinet approvaland is now part of the implementation policy of thisGovernment.

In the implementation of several foreign-funded projectsand local programmes including each and every programmeunder the “Mahinda Chintana”, this Ministry has developedsystems to capture information and to evaluate the progress.This has been done through a web-based system as well asthrough field visits undertaken by officers of our Ministry

ÀåÚÈèï¾àºëÉ10671068

[ªÇæ ÍêïÌà¾à ¡ÍÄ ÂÆúÈå ÄÍºå]as well as the Department of Foreign Aid and BudgetMonitoring, which comes under us. We have pursued follow-up action to ensure that any unsatisfactory factors areeliminated and the future programmes are improved basedon these findings.

During the course of next year, we will also focus on thenew projects that will be implemented at village level. The“Gama Neguma” programme highlights a much neededintervention which is designed to develop the countrythrough the development of a hitherto marginalized sectorof society. Through these programmes, the villagers will beempowered in a meaningful way, thereby contributingtowards the elimination of poverty in our country. Specialmonitoring and evaluation mechanisms have been put inplace and the Ministry is geared to review the progress so asto ensure these programmes are implemented effectively.

The Consultative Committee on the Ministry has beenmeeting very regularly every month and we have provideda forum to discuss issues that the Hon. Members of Parliamentwish to raise. I am grateful to all the Hon. Members ofParliament who have co-operated with us in the discharge ofour duties and functions and wish to ensure that we willcontinue to work with commitment in the next year as well.

I must also thank the two Additional Secretaries of myMinistry, Mr. Upali Dahanayake and Mr. M. I. M. Rafeek, forall the efforts they have made together with the Director-General of the Foreign Aid and Budget Monitoring Divisionand for the dedication and commitment they have shown inthe discharge of their functions. A special word of thanksmust go to the Secretary of the Ministry of Finance andPlanning, whose co-operation with our Ministry has madeour work much easier.

Thank you very much.

£Õ¶Æ¶¶Ç¯, ¥·Æ¶ ´»ºÆ ±ºÆ¹·Æ¶ºÇ¯ ·Ç ¥ÙºÆ ¬Î½¯Æç½ ÍÁ®ÕºÆ°

Sir, I have to say something about the regional radiostation. I must thank the Sri Lanka BroadcastingCorporation for having given us a Tamil FM channel, aregional services for the Ampara District where most ofthe Tamil people are now in a position to listen to the Tamilprogrammes. Under the name “Pirai FM”, we were able toestablish a regional radio station a year ago. I mustsincerely thank Mr. Panawennage, the Chief Engineer, whowas very helpful to me at that time when we started it. Imust also thank the Hon. Minister, the Hon. AnuraPriyadharshana Yapa, for having given all sorts of co-operation and Mr. Ganegala and Mr. Sunil Sarath Perera formaking that a success. But, I am very sorry to say thatthis has not been gazetted so far. The “Pirai FM” is theonly regional radio station that is earning a profit, as far asI understand. Therefore, this has to be gazetted and I amsorry to say that permanent employees have not beenappointed to this radio station. I hope and pray that theHon. Minister would take note of this matter I am referringto.

Also, for the Tamil Section of the Sri Lanka BroadcastingCorporation, a Director (National Service) has not beenappointed so far. When I spoke to the Chairman of the SriLanka Broadcasting Corporation, Mr. Sunil Sarath Perera,

he told me that they have already held an interview andare awaiting the Hon. Minister’s approval. They haveselected a person and we have not interfered with that. Butthe work of this National Service is suffering because thereis no Director appointed so far. So, I am requesting Mr.Ganegala also, who is here, to look into this matter andappoint a Director for the Tamil National Service of theSLBC so that they can air the programmes in a moresystematic and regular way.

£¶Æ×´ ¥±Æ ±·Æ¶¼Æ¹Æ¹¶Æ¶ÈÍ¾ I have to point out that Iregret very much to see that in our Ministry’s handoutnothing has been mentioned about allocating money forthe construction of a building for “Pirai FM.” We are nowoperating from a rented house and the landlord is askingfor that place.

I remember that in 2005 they allocated some money, butfinally, I do not know, something happened to that andthey were not able to do that. This time also, it is a verygrave omission, that it has not been included in theseproposals, but we should be able to do that with moneyallocated through a Supplementary Estimate in time to come.So, I wish to bring this to the notice of the Hon. Minister,the Hon. Anura Priyadharshana Yapa, to have “Pirai FM”gazetted and get us some funds for the construction of abuilding for “Pirai FM” to be aired in the Tamil-speakingareas.

I sincerely thank the Hon. Anura Priyadharshana Yapa,who has been very co-operative and congratulateMr. Ganegala who has held a number of workshops topromote the knowledge and activities of the journalists.The last one, we had in Ampara, a Tamil-speaking area. Weare trying to have a workshop in Batticaloa also.

ªÇæ ¦. ¦. ïÌàªë ¢Ì¾à ÄÍºå(ºÇ®ÚºÈÐ ©ºÆ° ©±Æ° Í±Ð ¥Ã¶É)(The Hon. M. H. Cegu Issadeen)

The Hon. Suresh Vadivel has asked that a workshop beheld in one of the districts in the hill country . He hadcome and asked the Hon. Minister, the Hon. AnuraPriyadharshana Yapa, that a workshop be held in the NuwaraEliya District. I hope Mr. Ganegala would make a note ofthis and have a workshop in Nuwara Eliya.

I see the Hon. Minister Athaulla here, who hasvolunteered to give us some funds for the construction of abuilding for “Pirai FM”. I thank him for attending itsfunctions: he participated in the first year anniversary. Hewas prepared to give us all sorts of help. I thank him verymuch.

I thank the Hon. Members of the Opposition for thecomments made and I am in agreement with most of whatthey said. I am also in agreement with what was said aboutthe suffering undergone by the Tamil people in Jaffna andI hope and pray that the President and the others wouldmake way for the opening of the A-9 so that the peoplewho are suffering in the Jaffna District, in the NorthernProvince, can have better lives.

I sincerely thank everybody.

ªÇæ ï°ÆÇåÙ Àò¾å¾àóÀêÈàïÈà ÄÍºå(ºÇ®ÚºÈÐ Ì²»¼Ç²Æ Ì¹¼Æ¸Ç·Æ×Ú¿ÆÍ¿)(The Hon. Jeyaraj Fernandopulle)Mr. Speaker, on behalf of the Prime Minister, Minister ofInternal Administration and Deputy Minister of Defence, Imove that, “Mr. Dayananda Dissanayake, Commissioner of elections,who retired from Government Service on 28.01.2002 was reappointedto the post of Commissioner of Elections with effect from 29.01.2002,on the salary he had been drawing at the time of retirement, underArticle 27 (2) of the 17th Amendment to the Constitution of theDemocratic Socialist Republic of Sri Lanka. This Parliament determinesthat the salary of the present Commissioner of Elections shall be revisedin terms of the provisions of the Public Administration Circulars No.15/2003, 9/2004 and 6/2006 on salary revisions which came intoeffect since then as personal to him, as follows :

01.01.2004Rs. 426,660/-(per year)01.12.2004Rs. 534,660/-(per year)01.01.2006Rs. 633,603/-(per year)01.01.2007Rs. 724,080/-(per year)

This Parliament further determines that the salary determined byParliament on 06.08.1997 by resolution as payable to the Commis-sioner of Elections shall be substituted by the salary determined by thisresolution incorporating the salary steps given therein as personal toMr. Dayananda Dissanayake.”

2007´ ¡ïÀà Çï Äªû ÀòÉåÍ¾Æ ¡åÇÃ ïÉÈå ¡ÉêÇæó 100Æú. 1907¼ûºÄÆú ¡ïÀà Çï Äªû ÀòÉåÍ¾ ïÌàÉÆ ¡åÇÃ ïÉÈå ºøïÂ¾àï¾à. ¦Ä ¾øÌå2007´ ¡ÉêÇæó 100Æú. ¡ÉêÇæó 100 ÌÀìÚ¸ É¾ ÉÚËïÆà¼û ¢¼úÖÆ´ ¡ïÀàÇï ÆÍÀºà Äªû ïÌàÉÆ¨à ¡åÇÃ ¨Ç ªæ¾ùÄ Ì¿Íå ï ÀåÚÈèï¾àºëÉ¾øïÆåà°¾Æ ¨Ç¾ ÌèÆõÄ ÄÍ°¾ ¾øïÆåàÔºÆ¾àïªà ÌÍïÆåàªÆ ¡À´ ÈæïÂ¾¡æºæÆú ÂÈåïÀåïÇåºàºë ïÉ¾à Äå ¾øÍ¹ ïÉ¾Éå.

[À. É. 5.13]

ªÇæ ¦à. ¦. ¦. ÏÉêÌè ÄÍºå (óÖÆ Íå ªÄ¾åªÄ¾ ¡ÄåºñºëÄåÌÍ ©¾ø° ïºÈà Íå ©¾ø° ïºÈà ÌÀºà ÌâÉÚ½¾ ¡ÄåºñºëÄå)(ºÇ®ÚºÈÐ ª° ©±Æ° ©ºÆ° Ì¹¿ÃÈ - ÚÎ¯¼¶ºÆ º½ÆÞºÆÍ¹Ç¯ÆÐÁ¼¶Æ× £Îº±Æ±ÝºÆ Ì¹½ÆÍ½Ç»ºÆ, Ì¹½ÆÍ½Ç» Á¿£Ý¶Æ¶È £Îº±Æ±ÝºÆ)(The Hon. A. H. M. Fowzie - Minister of Railways andTransport and Minister of Petroleum and Petroleum ResourcesDevelopment)Hon. Deputy Chairman of committees, I am very happy toparticipate in this Debate on the Adjournment Motion thisafternoon. The matter that has been raised by the Hon.Lakshman Yapa Abeywardena is very crucial. I must tell himthat he should undestand that during the 17-year period ofthe UNP Government, the entire Ceylon Transport Boardwas destroyed and the bus operations islandwide camevirtually to a grinding halt.The only policy of the thenGovernment was to sell the CTB against the wishers ofeveryone and ruin the public bus transport sector.

However, in 1994, when the PA Government took office,rapid changes and long lasting measures were introduced torectify the deteriorated state of the Sri Lanka Transport Board.during my time, all the dues such as the EPF, gratuitypayments et cetera, which had accumulated during the UNPregime, were paid to the employees at the time of theirretirement. That was when I was the Minister of Transportand Highways in 1997. However, during the very short periodthe UNP government took charge of governing this country,none of the payments in respect of gratuity and EPF due tothe employees was settled. Therefore, the present long-standing dues to the employees are those that had not beenpaid during the UNP regime. So , it was not our responsibility.Now it is ours because the Government will pay those. Butthese payments accumulated because the UNP regime didnot settle those.

Now, I wish to categorically stated the correct position. Itis not 14,000 employees. There are 3,900 employees of theformere cluster bus companies of the Sri Lanka TransportBoard who had retired and have not been paid their gratuityfor the period from 2002 to 2005. These payments shouldhave been made long time ago by those responsible to do so.But, it had not been done. These employees had served thecluster bus companies for a long period of time and weremade helpless at the time of their retirement when theirgratuity payments were not made by the employer.

The non-payment of gratuity to these employees has createdenormous problems for them. They are not in a position toeducate their children, to see their children settle in marriage,receive urgent medical care and settle other matters ofimportance in the domestic front. Therefore, after assumingoffice as the Minister of Railways and Transport, I tookimmediate steps to find ways and means of sorting out thishumane problem of the employees. As a matter of urgency,I submitted a Cabinet Paper regarding this matter and obtainedapproval of the Cabinet of Minister to make these payments.

12171218

ÀåÚÈèï¾àºëÉ

After having discussed this matter with the Secretary to theMinistry of finance and Planning, Parliament was presentedwith a Supplementary Estimate because no money wasprovided in the budget. Rs. 433.5 million was needed for thepayment of gratuity to employees of the former cluster buscompanies. The Supplementary Estimate was passed onlylast month and gratuity payments will be made very soon tothose affected employees. Even during the last few daysI was talking to the Secretary to the Ministry of Finance andPlanning. Dr. P. B. Jaeyasundera, asking for this money andhe promised to release it as quickly as possible. When I spoketo him today, he said that they had been busy with thepreparation of the Budget and they would release the moneywithin the course of next week or before the end of December.

It is our duty to see that these poor workers, who had retiredafter serving the country and the institution for a long time,are paid for the service they had rendered. These paymentsneed to be made very early since the affected employees aresuffering a lot and many had brought their grievances to mepersonallly and I am making every effort to pay them quickly.

The Hon. Lakshman Yapa Abeywardena made a statement,which I do not wish to challenge, but I will check it up. Wehave been paying in small installments of Rs. 10,000 andthis money which was handed over to the -

(Postage Rs. 2.50) Copies can be obtained by remitting in advance an annual subscription fee to theSUPERINTENDENT, GOVERNMENT PUBLICATION BUREAU, No. 32, Transworks House,Lotus Road, Colombo 1.
